How common is assessment cheating, and what do the estimates mean?

  • AI-assisted cheating in pre-employment assessments is reported as a material 2025-2026 integrity risk, but prevalence estimates vary sharply by study design and setting.our own page
  • Research estimates cited for cheating range from about 8% to 40%, with higher figures generally coming from studies that reward high scores rather than ordinary recruitment conditions.[1]182assessio.com
  • In a study of more than 500 practising candidates, fewer than 10% used a non-permitted tool and only 2.1% said they would consider using AI in a real assessment.[1]182assessio.com
  • Fabric's analysis of repeat interview candidates found three distinct patterns: 47% never cheated, 30% cheated in every interview, and 23% cheated only in some interviews.[13]183harrisbeachmurtha.com
  • Its data also reported the highest day-specific cheating rate on Sunday, at 47.1%, while other days clustered around roughly 35% to 40%.[13]183harrisbeachmurtha.com
  • In Fabric's reported cheating cases, dedicated assistants such as Cluely and Interview Coder accounted for 45%, LLM voice mode, including ChatGPT, accounted for 34%, tab switching or a second screen for 18%, and live help from another person made up the remainder.[13]183harrisbeachmurtha.com
  • In Fabric's reported cheating cases, dedicated assistants such as Cluely and Interview Coder accounted for 45%, LLM voice mode, including ChatGPT, accounted for 34%, tab switching or a second screen for 18%, and live help from another person made up the remainder.[13]183harrisbeachmurtha.com
  • In Fabric's reported cheating cases, dedicated assistants such as Cluely and Interview Coder accounted for 45%, LLM voice mode, including ChatGPT, accounted for 34%, tab switching or a second screen for 18%, and live help from another person made up the remainder.[13]183harrisbeachmurtha.com
  • In Fabric's reported cheating cases, dedicated assistants such as Cluely and Interview Coder accounted for 45%, LLM voice mode, including ChatGPT, accounted for 34%, tab switching or a second screen for 18%, and live help from another person made up the remainder.[13]183harrisbeachmurtha.com
  • A 2026 assessment-integrity summary reports that “one in three” candidates on monitored assessments attempted some form of fraud in 2025.our own page
  • It further reports that the rate among entry-level technical roles “approaches one in two.”our own page
  • The summary says it draws on three independent datasets published between February and March 2026, spanning structured coding platforms, AI-conducted interviews, and the wider online-exam market; however, the collected excerpt does not identify the underlying studies, sample sizes, or the exact fraud-attempt definitions used.[2]184linkedin.com
  • The same source says differing figures across sources were handled by reporting the most conservative figure, and distinguishes directly measured estimates from derived estimates.our own page
  • That methodological caveat matters because the reported figures aggregate different assessment formats and parts of the hiring funnel rather than representing one standardized industrywide measurement.[2]184linkedin.com
  • The 2026 assessment-integrity summary identifies structured coding platforms, AI-conducted interviews, and the broader online-exam market as distinct assessment-funnel slices represented in its datasets.our own page
  • It reports especially high attempted-fraud prevalence for entry-level technical roles, where the rate approaches one in two.[2]184linkedin.com
  • Live proctored coding assessments had a measured AI-fraud attempt rate of 35%–40% in CodeSignal’s 2025 data.[2]184linkedin.com
  • Live AI-conducted interviews had a measured fraud-attempt rate of 38.5% in Fabric’s 2025–2026 data.[2]184linkedin.com
  • Live human-conducted technical interviews without behavioral detection recorded fraud attempts of 48% or more, according to Fabric’s measurement.[2]184linkedin.com
  • Asynchronous take-home coding challenges are estimated to have a 60%–80% fraud rate.our own page
  • This is an estimate, not a directly measured rate: it is derived from CodeSignal’s finding that matched cohorts’ unproctored assessment scores increased by more than four times as much as proctored scores, combined with Fabric’s monitored-environment trajectory from 15% to 35% in six months.[2]184linkedin.com
  • Automated, no-time-pressure multiple-choice screening quizzes are estimated to face 70%–85% fraud, on the rationale that AI tools can solve many MCQ assessments within seconds.[2]184linkedin.com
  • The available evidence primarily measures proctored or AI-monitored environments.our own page
  • The assessment-specific estimate of one in three monitored candidates should not be conflated with broader hiring-fraud measures.our own page
  • In the wider recruitment funnel, nine in 10 HR workers reportedly saw a surge in low-effort, AI-generated applications in 2025; this measures reported application-volume pressure, not verified cheating on a skills assessment.[20]185support.shl.com
  • Gartner projects that one in four candidate profiles worldwide could be fake by 2028.our own page
  • Separately, Staffing Industry Analysts found that 41% of staffing buyers were already experiencing candidate-fraud challenges.our own page
  • Both figures concern candidate identity and profile fraud broadly, rather than a measured rate of AI-assisted cheating in a particular assessment.[20]185support.shl.com
  • The reported drivers of broader fraud are remote hiring, which lowers barriers to impersonation, and generative AI, which makes fabricated credentials, tailored resumes, and plausible interview responses inexpensive to create.[20]185support.shl.com
  • Background checks do not resolve the same measurement problem as assessment integrity.our own page
  • The collected information states that background checks are designed to assess whether someone is safe to hire, not whether the evaluated person is actually who they claim to be; it recommends moving identity verification earlier in the funnel, before the hiring decision is shaped.[20]185support.shl.com
  • The collected material identifies three independent datasets published between February and March 2026, covering structured coding platforms, AI-conducted interviews, and the broader online-exam market. It says these datasets converge on the conclusion that assessment fraud has become widespread, but it does not provide their study names, sample sizes, recruitment methods, denominators, full results tables, or direct links in the collected extract.[2]184linkedin.com
  • One source reports that, in 2025, one in three candidates on monitored assessments attempted some form of fraud.our own page
  • It further states that the rate for entry-level technical roles approaches one in two.our own page
  • The extract does not define “attempted,” identify the monitored assessment provider(s), distinguish AI assistance from other misconduct, or provide confidence intervals or detection methodology.[2]184linkedin.com
  • Assessio reports a substantially lower result from a study of more than 500 applicants: 10% used a tool that was not permitted, and 2.1% said they would consider using AI in a real assessment.our own page
  • This is self-reported evidence, so it measures reported behavior or stated willingness rather than independently verified AI-assisted cheating.[1]182assessio.com
  • The material describes the high-risk evidence landscape as spanning structured coding platforms, AI-conducted interviews, and the broader online-exam market.our own page
  • However, the extract supplies no format-specific prevalence estimates for coding tests, asynchronous video interviews, work samples, cognitive tests, knowledge exams, take-home exercises, or simulation-based assessments.[2]184linkedin.com
  • The prevalence figures are not directly comparable. The “one in three” and “approaches one in two” figures concern fraud attempts on monitored assessments, while Assessio’s 10% figure concerns self-reported use of any unpermitted tool among more than 500 applicants, and its 2.1% figure concerns willingness to use AI in a real assessment.[2]184linkedin.com
  • The collected evidence does not consistently distinguish among AI-assisted answer generation, AI-mediated impersonation, external human assistance, unauthorized devices or tabs, plagiarism, deepfakes, and other misconduct.our own page
  • This prevents a precise estimate of generative-AI cheating specifically.[2]184linkedin.com
  • Most cited evidence lacks essential study detail in the extract: named researchers or publishers, sampling frame, sample size, participant geography, role seniority, assessment duration, assessment format, fraud definition, observation period, validation method, and uncertainty estimates.[2]184linkedin.com
  • Academic-exam findings, including the 70% versus 15% proctoring comparison, should not be assumed to transfer directly to high-stakes pre-employment assessments without evidence from comparable candidate populations, hiring consequences, device environments, and incentive structures.[15]150pin.com

How candidates use AI and other hidden assistance

  • The 2025-2026 evidence describes AI-assisted cheating as behaviorally different from traditional forms: it may leave no visible tab switch, paste event, or physical note-taking signal.[2]184linkedin.com
  • Invisible-overlay tools can render answer content only on the candidate's local display, while Zoom, Teams, or Google Meet screen sharing captures the desktop beneath the overlay.[2]184linkedin.com
  • Interview Coder is described as a $100 lifetime product claiming 100,000+ users and no documented detections when properly used; its listed limitation is inability to adapt to follow-up questions mid-solution.[2]184linkedin.com
  • Interview Coder is described as a $100 lifetime product claiming 100,000+ users and no documented detections when properly used; its listed limitation is inability to adapt to follow-up questions mid-solution.[2]184linkedin.com
  • Cluely is listed at $20 per month and uses an invisible overlay plus audio pipeline; because its cloud architecture sends transcripts and session data through vendor servers, it may be vulnerable to network-layer blocking of LLM API calls.[2]184linkedin.com
  • Cluely is listed at $20 per month and uses an invisible overlay plus audio pipeline; because its cloud architecture sends transcripts and session data through vendor servers, it may be vulnerable to network-layer blocking of LLM API calls.[2]184linkedin.com
  • If candidates use their own local IDE for a take-home assessment, GitHub Copilot, Cursor, or Codeium can generate code inside the IDE.our own page
  • Candidates can use generative AI to produce interview answers or code in real time, including through tools that are invisible to Zoom, Teams, Google Meet, or ordinary screen sharing.our own page
  • These overlays render only on the candidate’s local display through low-level graphics hooks, while the shared video captures the desktop beneath the overlay.[13]183harrisbeachmurtha.com
  • Cluely, advertised at $20 per month, combines an invisible overlay with an audio pipeline; its cloud-dependent design means transcripts and session data pass through vendor servers.[2]184linkedin.com
  • Interview Coder, advertised at $100 lifetime and claiming 100,000+ users, is described as invisible in Activity Monitor and the dock; its stated limitation is that it cannot adapt to follow-up questions in the middle of a solution.[2]184linkedin.com
  • Open-source alternatives can be renamed or rebuilt to avoid process- or signature-based detection.our own page
  • OpenCluely is described as a customizable local-AI overlay;our own page
  • Pluely’s source code can reportedly be renamed and recompiled in under an hour;our own page
  • Natively can disguise its process as Terminal, Activity Monitor, or System Settings;our own page
  • and a functional custom overlay can reportedly be assembled in about two hours from Tesseract OCR, Whisper speech-to-text, and the Gemini API.[2]184linkedin.com
  • AI code-generation tools embedded in a candidate’s own IDE, including GitHub Copilot, Cursor, and Codeium, can generate implementation from a typed comment.our own page
  • Because the code can appear to be typed normally, this method may leave no copy-paste event, tab switch, or visible external application.[5]181testlify.com
  • A browser-based assessment IDE can prevent local IDE integrations, and desktop-locking controls can prevent candidates from opening a local IDE, but such controls apply only where the testing environment is locked down.[5]181testlify.com
  • Network-layer enforcement may block cloud-dependent tools that need LLM API calls, but it cannot reliably identify custom-built or locally run overlays by name or binary signature.[2]184linkedin.com
  • A candidate can keep a phone, tablet, second laptop, notes, or other reference material outside the webcam frame.our own page
  • One described 2026 pattern is a tablet placed beneath the desk running ChatGPT, with the candidate periodically looking down to read generated answers.[5]181testlify.com
  • Webcam-only monitoring has a physical blind spot: a device below the camera frame may not be visible.our own page
  • Gaze tracking can flag repeated off-screen or downward eye movement,our own page
  • randomized webcam snapshots can capture a candidate mid-glance,our own page
  • and mobile-phone detection can flag devices that do enter the frame.[5]181testlify.com
  • For higher-stakes assessments, dual-camera proctoring, using a laptop camera plus a phone camera aimed at the workspace, is presented as a way to reduce those blind spots;our own page
  • audio monitoring may identify candidates reading answers aloud from a second device.[5]181testlify.com
  • A room scan at the start of a session can identify obvious secondary screens, but not necessarily a phone under the desk.our own page
  • Webcam and microphone monitoring can flag whispered conversations, although audio-analysis accuracy varies and background noise can create false positives.[24]68wearedevelopers.com
  • Real-time voice assistance can be hard to detect through audio alone.our own page
  • The evidence states that by 2024, voice cloning required about 30 seconds of sample audio, and that by 2026 AirPods-style earbuds with on-device LLM assistants were mainstream consumer hardware; silent or sub-audible assistance defeats approaches that depend on audible coaching.[27]186disa.com

What signals and evidence can support a cheating investigation?

  • Visible behavioral signals still occur, but should be interpreted as patterns rather than proof.our own page
  • CodeSignal's 2025 flagged sessions showed frequent off-screen referencing in 35% of sessions and unusually linear typing patterns in 23%.[2]184linkedin.com
  • Frequent mouse-outs on every question may be a strong indicator, whereas a few isolated mouse-outs do not strongly indicate cheating.[14]66shl.com
  • Session flags alone can reflect innocent conduct, including looking down while thinking or background noise from roommates, and evidence should be reviewed before a decision.[6]187fabrichq.ai
  • Fabric describes analyzing more than 20 signals during an interview, including gaze patterns, response-time variance, language patterns typical of LLM output, and coherence against the candidate's resume baseline, then combining them into a probability score.[3]188aiseptor.com
  • Fabric reports an 85% cheating-detection rate and timestamped reports for recruiter verification, but this is a vendor-reported evaluation rather than an independent benchmark in the collected material.[3]188aiseptor.com
  • Speaker-diarisation systems such as NVIDIA NeMo and pyannote can detect a second voice that persists beyond a configured threshold.our own page
  • Transcription with Whisper or NeMo Parakeet can flag phrases such as “just give me the answer” or “what is question 7”; the same audio signal may capture a semi-audible AI earbud assistant.[27]186disa.com
  • Background-voice detection, conversation patterns, and randomized webcam snapshots can support an investigation into a second person assisting from the room.our own page
  • A plagiarism check may also identify identical or near-identical submissions among candidates who received the same answers.[5]181testlify.com
  • Testlify lists unexpected voices and talking as real-time suspicious-activity signals, while its proctoring controls can preserve snapshots and session recordings for later review.[6]187fabrichq.ai
  • Automata’s published candidate-data terms describe AI-based results including Face Not Matched, Multiple Voice Detection, Multiple Face Detection, and No-Face Detection.our own page
  • Its final conduct data can also include high similarity to internet content, other participants’ content, or AI-generated content; multi-line insertion of content or code; machine-switching restrictions; and code replay for coding assessments.[17]169staffinghub.com
  • Collect question-level time data and use it as context.our own page
  • Excessively short or long responses, or unusual timing patterns, may indicate AI use, but time data cannot serve as standalone proof of cheating.[14]66shl.com
  • Track behavioral signals such as whether the mouse leaves the test window, which may indicate use of another tab or browser.[14]66shl.com
  • These monitoring methods identify suspected cheating after the assessment, not the candidate's unaided ability; a monitoring-first approach may remove candidates who used assistance even when they might otherwise have been strong hires.[14]66shl.com
  • Very short completion times can also cast doubt on score meaning.our own page

Why automated detection requires human review and fair procedures

  • AI can be used to write cover letters, written responses, and other recruitment materials.our own page
  • The collected evidence cautions that AI-text detectors are unreliable, particularly against newer ChatGPT versions.our own page
  • OpenAI discontinued its AI Text Classifier in July 2023 because it was inaccurate.[26]189forasoft.com
  • A Stanford study described in the evidence found that more than half of writing samples from non-native English speakers were misclassified as AI-generated by automated detectors, while native samples were identified accurately.[8]190hackerearth.com
  • Another cited Stanford 2023 result reports GPTZero at 61% accuracy on student writing and a 26% false-positive rate against non-native English speakers.[27]186disa.com
  • The same material states that commercial AI-text detectors score below 60% accuracy in independent benchmarks and have double-digit false-positive rates.[27]186disa.com
  • Writing patterns such as repeated paragraph starters, repeated words, unnecessary buzzwords, or unusually polished vocabulary may be prompts for further inquiry, but they are not reliable proof of AI use.[26]189forasoft.com
  • The more defensible evidence described in the collection is authorial attestation, draft history, behavioral signals, and a candidate’s ability to explain or vary their own work in a live follow-up.[25]69integrityadvocate.com
  • AI-text detectors should not be the basis of an academic-integrity or candidate-integrity finding.our own page
  • The collected material cites Stanford’s 2023 measurement of 61% accuracy and a 26% false-positive rate against non-native English writers, notes that Turnitin walked back earlier claims in 2023, and states that OpenAI shut down its classifier.[27]186disa.com
  • The RAID benchmark evaluation from ACL 2024 found that standalone detectors perform well on clean, unedited AI text but degrade under student revision, mixed human-AI writing, and domain shifts.[9]191meazurelearning.com
  • A follow-up study cited in the collected material reported a mean false-positive rate of 61.3% for TOEFL essays by Chinese students, compared with 5.1% for US essays in the same setup.[9]191meazurelearning.com
  • The same source describes an original-work case that received a 30.76% probability score and initially led to a misconduct accusation before the teacher recognized the error.[9]191meazurelearning.com
  • Where an AI-text score exists, it should prompt further investigation: compare the work with the candidate’s prior work, inspect drafting and keystroke evidence, ask process questions, and document the reasoning.our own page
  • The cited protocol frames this as a fairer and more defensible record than treating a probability score as proof.[9]191meazurelearning.com
  • The source characterizes this combination as “bulletproof,” but that is a vendor-style claim rather than independent proof of perfect prevention.[14]66shl.com
  • Treat automated flags as leads, not decisions.our own page
  • The collected information argues that every flagged session should receive trained human review before an outcome is issued, producing a documented record of what was observed, evaluated, and concluded.[8]190hackerearth.com
  • Ask whether every flagged session receives human review before an outcome at every pricing tier, because optional review can leave most flagged sessions unreviewed and turn flags into outcomes.[8]190hackerearth.com
  • Eye-tracking heuristics can flag candidates whose gaze repeatedly moves off-screen, but the collected material describes this as a signal rather than proofour own page
  • and recommends a follow-up interview rather than rejection.[24]68wearedevelopers.com
  • Audio analysis may flag whispered conversations, but background noise can produce false positives.[24]68wearedevelopers.com
  • Eye-tracking and audio-based flags have meaningful false-positive rates, particularly for candidates with disabilities, shared living spaces, or thinking styles that involve looking away from the screen.[24]68wearedevelopers.com
  • Webcam-based proctoring has documented false-positive rates that disproportionately affect candidates with darker skin tones, certain disabilities, and non-ideal testing environments.[24]68wearedevelopers.com
  • Stanford research published in *Cell Press* found that automated detectors misclassified more than half of writing samples from non-native English speakers as AI-generated, while identifying native-English samples accurately;our own page
  • the source applies the same concern to proctoring systems that act on flags without human review.[8]190hackerearth.com
  • For potential off-camera assistance, suggested measures include a 360-degree room scan at the beginning of the session, webcam and microphone monitoring throughout the assessment, audio analysis to flag possible whispered conversations, and eye-tracking heuristics that flag repeatedly off-screen gaze.[24]68wearedevelopers.com
  • These methods have limits: room scans can catch obvious secondary screens but may not identify a phone under a desk; audio analysis accuracy varies and background noise can create false positives.[24]68wearedevelopers.com
  • These methods have limits: room scans can catch obvious secondary screens but may not identify a phone under a desk; audio analysis accuracy varies and background noise can create false positives.[24]68wearedevelopers.com
  • Eye-tracking flags are characterized as signals rather than proof and should prompt a follow-up interview, not an automatic rejection.[24]68wearedevelopers.com
  • SHL advises candidates whose online assessment freezes because of an interrupted internet connection not to click “Exit,” because doing so can submit responses already entered and leave no opportunity to finish if time remains; candidates should refresh or reload the assessment page, and contact technical support if they clicked Exit accidentally.[23]135xobin.com
  • SHL advises candidates whose online assessment freezes because of an interrupted internet connection not to click “Exit,” because doing so can submit responses already entered and leave no opportunity to finish if time remains; candidates should refresh or reload the assessment page, and contact technical support if they clicked Exit accidentally.[23]135xobin.com
  • This illustrates the need for procedures that separate technical failure from assessment misconduct.[23]135xobin.com

Which assessment formats are most exposed to AI assistance?

  • Timed cognitive tests are exposed to unauthorized calculators, search engines, and AI tools, while personality, motivation, and values assessments are more exposed to faking or misrepresentation than cheating.[1]182assessio.com
  • The collected evidence indicates that AI does not affect all item formats equally.our own page
  • Assessio reports relatively stronger AI performance on verbal and numerical items but 44% accuracy on figural questions, below average human performance on important assessment criteria. This suggests that image-based or figural reasoning tasks may be less exposed to generic text-based AI assistance than verbal and numerical formats, although the extract does not provide human accuracy figures, task design, or model-specific results.[1]182assessio.com
  • The central distinction is whether the assessment is designed to measure unaided performance, real-world performance with tools, or the ability to use AI effectively; employers should define this before testing and should not make integrity judgments after running a vague process.[54]67linkedin.com
  • When candidates can use AI to complete an assessment that is supposed to measure independent knowledge or reasoning, their results may reflect access to a chatbot rather than their own competence.our own page
  • One source argues that if AI can achieve 90% on an employer’s current test, the test may be measuring the wrong thing; it recommends placing more weight on judgment, critical thinking, communication under ambiguity, and creative problem-solving, where generic AI output may be easier for experienced evaluators to distinguish from genuine depth.[25]69integrityadvocate.com
  • Multiple-choice formats appear more exposed than scenario-based tasks.our own page
  • By contrast, assessment formats in which AI assistance provides little advantage are presented as preserving score interpretability because candidates perform closer to their actual ability and scores better reflect genuine capability.[14]66shl.com
  • The implication is that AI-assisted distortion of a well-validated cognitive or skills assessment can be particularly consequential because it compromises a signal that may be stronger than résumé-based screening.our own page

How AI-assisted scores affect hiring decisions and assessment design

  • AI assistance can undermine the validity of a pre-employment assessment when the score no longer represents the capability the assessment was intended to measure.our own page
  • A source on hiring practice reports that employers are increasingly favoring behavioral interviews, skills tests, and assessments over polished written submissions because AI-assisted resumes have weakened confidence in resumes as evidence of capability.our own page
  • In a 2026 Willo study of more than 100 hiring professionals worldwide, supplemented with insights from 2.5 million candidate interviews on Willo’s platform, 37% of employers considered credentials and learning history among the most reliable talent indicators; 41% were actively moving away from resume-first hiring; 10% had largely replaced resumes with skills-based and scenario-driven assessments; and about 15% were exploring alternatives.our own page
  • These figures document changing employer behavior, not the cheating prevalence or validity of the replacement assessment formats.[39]85techrseries.com
  • Time limits can reduce opportunities to seek outside help or search for answers, while also standardizing conditions across candidates, but time pressure alone does not establish whether a candidate actually has the measured skill.[30]64incruiter.com
  • Follow-up verification can reveal inflated scores, but it cannot fully repair an invalid initial screen.our own page
  • If many candidates used AI to enter the finalist pool, then weaker but genuine candidates may already have been screened out before verification occurs.[14]66shl.com
  • Verification assessments also impose administrative cost because every finalist must complete an additional assessment, adding time to an already demanding hiring stage.[14]66shl.com
  • Monitoring-based approaches similarly identify suspected cheating after the assessment rather than ensuring the original score represents genuine ability.our own page
  • They may remove candidates who used AI, including candidates who could otherwise have been strong hires, but they do not establish how capable those candidates actually are.[14]66shl.com

What signals can flag potential assessment fraud?proctoring assessment KD 0 · vol 110

Assessment performance and completion patterns

  • Short completion time is another cited signal: assessments that typically take 25 to 30 minutes but are completed in under 10 minutes may indicate AI-assisted or otherwise inauthentic performance.our own page

Limits of webcam and desktop recording

  • Traditional webcam or desktop recording can deter attempts, but it raises privacy concerns, increases candidate drop-off, creates accessibility issues, harms employer brand, and can still be bypassed by a phone kept off-screen.[14]66shl.com

How can hiring assessments preserve integrity in the age of AI assistance?differentiatorno keyword

Design assessment formats that are harder to outsource

  • AI performs well on verbal and numerical questions but reportedly scores only 44% on figural questions, below the average human.[1]182assessio.com
  • Strict time limits can make switching applications impractical, reducing the usefulness of external AI assistance in those tests.[1]182assessio.com
  • Static take-home assignments are described as increasingly measuring AI literacy rather than the candidate's own skill; one proposed response is to evaluate how candidates used AI rather than whether they used it, or replace take-homes with live coding sessions that show problem solving.[3]188aiseptor.com
  • Static take-home assignments are described as increasingly measuring AI literacy rather than the candidate's own skill; one proposed response is to evaluate how candidates used AI rather than whether they used it, or replace take-homes with live coding sessions that show problem solving.[3]188aiseptor.com
  • Interactive, time-sensitive gamified assessments are harder to use with AI because the screen changes continuously and there is no stable question to copy into ChatGPT and answer later.[14]66shl.com
  • Structured behavioral simulations, such as timed scenarios involving an angry parent, team conflict, budget trade-off, or student-safety decision, test judgment under ambiguity and are presented as harder to outsource to AI than cover letters or rehearsed interview responses.[4]192testpartnership.com
  • Their resistance comes from the task structure: the candidate must reason through a changing, timed situation in real time.[4]192testpartnership.com
  • Scenario-based assessments may expose a different measurement pattern than multiple-choice questions.our own page
  • Most technical assessments globally are described as lacking dedicated proctoring, including take-home assignments, asynchronous coding challenges, and automated screening tests that depend on time limits and the honor system.[2]184linkedin.com
  • Take-home projects and code assignments allow direct use of ChatGPT, Claude, and Copilot without an overlay, time constraint, or monitoring layer.[2]184linkedin.com
  • In a take-home or written case study, a candidate can paste the prompt into ChatGPT, refine the output, and submit work produced through roughly an hour of prompting rather than the eight hours of human reasoning the exercise was intended to measure.[4]192testpartnership.com
  • Behavioral questionnaires are similarly exposed: for prompts such as “Tell us about a time when you faced a conflict with a colleague,” a model can generate a high-scoring answer in a candidate-trained voice before the candidate has finished reading the question.[4]192testpartnership.com
  • Static assessments, including take-home tests and standardized coding challenges, are described as predictable environments that give cheating tools a stable setting in which to operate.our own page
  • Conversational interviews can instead adapt follow-up questions to a candidate’s responses, probing for specifics, personal experiences, and edge cases.[3]188aiseptor.com
  • Live interviews can be targeted with real-time AI assistance.our own page
  • Live FaceCode-style interviews that require system-design diagrams and on-the-fly thinking are presented as harder for copilot tools to replicate than static coding tasks.[5]181testlify.com
  • AI-conducted conversational interviews can change questions dynamically in response to an answer, rather than asking fixed questions.our own page
  • This creates a moving target for external answer-generation tools and requires the candidate to demonstrate understanding interactively.[3]188aiseptor.com
  • Question leakage and reused prompts create another route to unauthorized help.our own page
  • One cited approach uses randomized item banks, adaptive testing, and a question bank of more than 180,000 validated questions refreshed every three months to limit leakage and pattern exploitation.[25]69integrityadvocate.com
  • Adaptive item banks can make questions less predictable, but they do not by themselves prevent real-time AI use because candidates can still enter questions into AI tools and receive answers.our own page
  • They need to be combined with controls aimed specifically at AI-assisted cheating.[14]66shl.com
  • A one-time access window, timed sections, randomized equivalent-difficulty questions, follow-up video questions asking candidates to explain their answers, and restrictions on copying questions into Google or ChatGPT can reduce opportunities for outside help while preserving comparable testing conditions.[30]64incruiter.com
  • Adaptive conversational interviews can create additional investigative evidence because follow-up questions can probe personal experience, specifics, edge cases, and the reasoning behind a polished answer.our own page
  • Fabric argues that this makes static, predictable assessments easier to cheat than interviews that adapt to the candidate’s responses.[3]188aiseptor.com
  • For take-home work, the same source recommends either evaluating how candidates used AI or replacing the assignment with live coding that exposes problem-solving process.[3]188aiseptor.com
  • Assessment vulnerability differs by format: AI-assisted manipulation is growing, especially in written formats, while assessments that measure observable behavior or actual capability are described as harder to game.[35]125clevry.com
  • Use job simulations when practical.our own page
  • The design objective is to reduce the value of AI assistance before relying on surveillance.our own page
  • When AI assistance provides no meaningful advantage, scores can more closely reflect actual ability and fewer candidates need to be removed after assessment for assistance that changed the result.[14]66shl.com
  • Gamified assessments combined with verification tests are presented as one design pattern: use the gamified assessment for the initial screen, then a more traditional verification assessment for variety and confirmation.[14]66shl.com
  • Assessment design that measures direct skills and behavior rather than CV signals can reduce reliance on information AI can enhance or distort.[35]125clevry.com
  • Sequential verification is recommended when written submissions are used: candidates should be asked in real time to extend, defend, and build on their submission.[25]69integrityadvocate.com
  • The collected evidence argues that the difference between a candidate who genuinely authored a response and one who pasted AI-generated output can become apparent within the first two follow-up questions.[25]69integrityadvocate.com
  • Video prompts that ask candidates to explain how they arrived at answers can confirm understanding and reveal how effectively they communicate their thinking, a skill relevant to job performance.[30]64incruiter.com
  • This approach matters because a candidate who used AI to prepare is not necessarily equivalent to a candidate who used AI to simulate a capability they do not possess.[54]67linkedin.com

Set clear AI-use rules and match controls to assessment stakes

  • A layered approach combines assessment design with technical and human review.our own page
  • Configurable controls can vary by assessment stakes, including violation limits, snapshot intervals, warnings, flags, and session-ending rules.[6]187fabrichq.ai
  • Human involvement can reduce preventable integrity problems before an assessment starts.our own page
  • A hybrid model, in which AI flags events and humans decide, is recommended in the collected material for midterms, finals, university entrance exams, and corporate certifications; AI-only monitoring is positioned for low-stakes or high-volume testing, while human-only review is positioned for the highest-stakes professional examinations.[7]109linkedin.com
  • The ethical status of AI use in job interviews remains context-dependent: a February 2026 Built In article framed the question “Is Using AI in a Job Interview Cheating?” as depending on context, reflecting rapidly changing candidate-side norms.[5]181testlify.com
  • Stronger monitoring should be proportionate to the stakes: a short screening test may suit light monitoring, while a final-round assessment may justify stricter limits and stronger evidence.our own page
  • Configurable settings can include warning thresholds, flagging thresholds, session-ending rules, violation limits, snapshot intervals, and individual monitoring controls.[6]187fabrichq.ai
  • The detection stack should match the stakes of the assessment.our own page
  • Testlify recommends lighter monitoring for short screening tests and stricter controls, lower violation limits, different snapshot intervals, or session termination rules for final-round assessments.[6]187fabrichq.ai
  • Higher-control measures create friction and must be supported by clear evidence.our own page
  • Most proctoring platforms require a webcam, microphone, stable internet of at least 2 Mbps, and a modern browser; InCruiter identifies those as baseline requirements.[31]193aiseptor.com
  • Use clear pre-assessment warnings.our own page
  • Candidates can be asked to confirm that they will not use external help and told that behavior may be monitored or verified later; the collected material says these warnings can reduce AI use because many candidates will not take the risk if they believe detection is plausible.[14]66shl.com
  • Willo’s 2026 report identifies a shift away from relying on polished resumes as AI-assisted applications became common.our own page
  • Employers increasingly favor behavioral interviews, skills tests, and assessments over written submissions; the report draws on responses from more than 100 hiring professionals worldwide, 2.5 million candidate interviews on Willo’s platform, and hiring-expert analysis from organizations including Toyota GB and Microsoft.[39]85techrseries.com
  • Employers increasingly favor behavioral interviews, skills tests, and assessments over written submissions; the report draws on responses from more than 100 hiring professionals worldwide, 2.5 million candidate interviews on Willo’s platform, and hiring-expert analysis from organizations including Toyota GB and Microsoft.[39]85techrseries.com
  • Willo CEO Euan Cameron described the concern that resumes may now show “how well someone can prompt a large language model,” and said employers are seeking “real signals of capability” beyond summaries of experience.[39]85techrseries.com
  • Willo CEO Euan Cameron described the concern that resumes may now show “how well someone can prompt a large language model,” and said employers are seeking “real signals of capability” beyond summaries of experience.[39]85techrseries.com
  • Employers can distinguish between AI uses they permit and uses they restrict.our own page
  • Suggested controls include publishing AI-use rules on the employer’s or third-party job portal, tailoring notices to roles with specific rules, requiring candidates to attest that they did not use AI during an application or to disclose their use, and giving candidates information about what will happen if they violate the rules.[44]194klgates.com
  • Suggested controls include publishing AI-use rules on the employer’s or third-party job portal, tailoring notices to roles with specific rules, requiring candidates to attest that they did not use AI during an application or to disclose their use, and giving candidates information about what will happen if they violate the rules.[44]194klgates.com
  • Suggested controls include publishing AI-use rules on the employer’s or third-party job portal, tailoring notices to roles with specific rules, requiring candidates to attest that they did not use AI during an application or to disclose their use, and giving candidates information about what will happen if they violate the rules.[44]194klgates.com
  • Suggested controls include publishing AI-use rules on the employer’s or third-party job portal, tailoring notices to roles with specific rules, requiring candidates to attest that they did not use AI during an application or to disclose their use, and giving candidates information about what will happen if they violate the rules.[44]194klgates.com
  • The same guidance identifies potentially acceptable uses, such as AI-generated interview-preparation questions or AI editing of resumes and cover letters, versus potentially problematic uses such as drafting resumes or cover letters from scratch, drafting or editing writing samples, or answering interview questions.[44]194klgates.com
  • The same guidance identifies potentially acceptable uses, such as AI-generated interview-preparation questions or AI editing of resumes and cover letters, versus potentially problematic uses such as drafting resumes or cover letters from scratch, drafting or editing writing samples, or answering interview questions.[44]194klgates.com
  • The broader assessment principle is that integrity requires clear rules, clear instructions, role-relevant design, and actual verification before accusations, consistent with NIST guidance emphasizing documented testing, evaluation, verification, and validation rather than assumption-based judgment.[54]67linkedin.com
  • Controls should therefore be proportionate to assessment stakes.our own page
  • The collected material recommends time limits and stricter controls where needed, confirming that the assessment works across candidates’ desktop, laptop, and mobile devices, and protecting integrity without unnecessary friction for honest candidates.[6]187fabrichq.ai
  • Privacy and compliance also affect validity in practice: employers should know how assessment data are stored, who can access it, and which standards the vendor follows.[6]187fabrichq.ai
  • The evidence supports a layered approach: adaptive item banks, non-intrusive monitoring such as time-recorded scoring and mouse tracking, applicant agreements and AI warnings, and verification tests where traditional assessments remain in use.[14]66shl.com
  • This combination aims to preserve the meaning of scores at the initial screen while avoiding the conclusion that an automated signal, a polished submission, or mere AI use alone proves either cheating or job competence.our own page

Use layered proctoring and collect reviewable evidence

  • Recommended evidence for reviewing a flagged assessment includes session recordings, snapshots, question-level activity logs, timestamps, and plain-language violation summaries.[6]187fabrichq.ai
  • Audio monitoring can identify background voices; randomized webcam snapshots may capture another person; and plagiarism checking can identify identical or near-identical submissions.[5]181testlify.com
  • Custom per-question timers, automatic logout after a candidate leaves the webcam frame beyond a configured threshold, and full-screen lockdown are suggested controls for unmonitored exits such as restroom breaks.[5]181testlify.com
  • One provider’s proctoring data includes AI-generated indicators such as face-not-matched, multiple-voice detection, multiple-face detection, and no-face detection.our own page
  • Its conduct-data factors also include high similarity between responses and internet, other-participant, or AI-available content; multi-line insertion of content or code; machine-switch restrictions; and code replay for Automata assessments.[17]169staffinghub.com
  • Assessment platforms can measure multiple forms of possible third-party or AI assistance.our own page
  • These measures are indicators rather than a direct prevalence estimate.our own page
  • The provider describes them as data used to determine the likelihood of third-party assistance, including AI systems, and says the employer elects which conduct factors to review.[17]169staffinghub.com
  • AI proctoring monitors a remote assessment, verifies that the candidate is the claimed person, watches for unauthorized assistance, flags unusual behavior in real time, and stores evidence for later review. Testlify characterizes its broader integrity framework as six layers: identity assurance, environment control, behavior monitoring, AI-assistance detection, reviewable evidence, and configurable strictness; final judgment remains human-led.[6]187fabrichq.ai
  • Common delivery models are automated AI proctoring, live human proctoring, record-and-review, and hybrid proctoring. Automated proctoring flags suspicious activity without a human watching live and is positioned for volume; live proctoring suits smaller, high-stakes cohorts; record-and-review is a middle ground; hybrid models use AI across sessions with human review of flags or live escalation when needed.[6]187fabrichq.ai
  • Criteria’s AI proctoring workflow captures a candidate image before the assessment, takes periodic image, screen, and audio samples during the session, flags anomalies, and produces a report with flagged incidents and supporting evidence for reviewer decisions.[21]195hackerearth.com
  • Criteria’s stated evidence types include periodic image capture for candidate presence; continuous facial-recognition analysis to confirm the same candidate remains present and to detect mobile-device use; screen and ambient-audio snippets to detect unauthorized tools or outside help; and transparent reporting for review.[22]196hackerearth.com
  • SHL’s proctoring category can collect pause time; restrict or log copy, print, and paste; restrict and count browser toggles and print-screen events; and log toggles to other websites. Where enabled by the employer, it can also use live audio-video monitoring, periodic audio/still-image/video capture, multi-face and no-face detection, suspicious-object detection such as a mobile phone, face verification, ID-document recording, and multi-voice detection.[17]169staffinghub.com
  • SHL states that its proctoring analysis can include high-similarity scores against internet content, other participants’ content, or AI-generated content; multi-line insertion of content or code; machine-switch restrictions; and code replay for Automata assessments. Its AI-based results can include Face Not Matched, Multiple Voice Detection, Multiple Face Detection, and No-Face Detection, which become part of the candidate’s reported Conduct Data.[17]169staffinghub.com
  • Browser-based assessment environments can remove some local-IDE risk. HackerEarth Assessments is described as using a browser-based IDE, preventing Copilot integration, while Smart Browser is described as locking the desktop environment to prevent candidates from opening a local IDE or other applications.[5]181testlify.com
  • Candidate preparation matters: SHL says its assessments include instructions and an example screenshot before the real test so candidates know what they will see and be required to do.[23]135xobin.com
  • Video and audio assessment formats expand the data collected and analyzed. SHL’s audio assessments can analyze pronunciation against a selected neutral-accent benchmark and speech disfluencies, including unnatural pauses, rate, and flow; numerical features are compared with benchmarks and passed through an AI computational model to generate results.[17]169staffinghub.com
  • SHL’s advanced video assessments can collect video image, audio responses, video recordings, practical online exercises or project work, and AI-based speech-to-text transcriptions.[17]169staffinghub.com
  • Criteria AI Proctoring likewise describes post-assessment reports containing flagged incidents and supporting evidence for a team to review.[21]195hackerearth.com
  • A YOLO-class object detector can inspect every nth video frame for phones, second laptops, or paper notes.our own page
  • The cited design recommends tuning this detector for high recall, accepting false positives such as hands resting on a desk because a reviewer can dismiss them, while missed phone detections are more costly.[27]186disa.com
  • A tablet placed beneath the desk can remain outside a standard webcam frame while a candidate repeatedly glances downward to read AI-generated answers.our own page
  • Suggested evidence sources include gaze tracking, phone detection when a device enters the frame, randomized webcam snapshots, audio evidence if answers are read aloud, and, for high-stakes assessments, a second phone camera aimed at the workspace.[5]181testlify.com
  • Periodic image, screen, and audio sampling can identify unauthorized resources, second devices, or outside assistance, although it produces samples rather than continuous evidence.[21]195hackerearth.com
  • Video proctoring can also record candidate behavior and help identify visible unauthorized cell phones or additional computers.[29]197canditech.io
  • Candidates leaving the webcam frame can be logged against a configured time threshold, with automatic logout after an extended absence.our own page
  • Question-level timers keep the clock running during an absence, and full-screen controls can flag leaving the assessment screen.[5]181testlify.com
  • Relevant session evidence includes tab and window switches, full-screen exits, copy-paste events, mouse-out activity, screen changes, and question-level activity logs.[30][6]64187incruiter.comfabrichq.ai
  • Network and device signals include the same physical device used by two test-takers within an hour, simultaneous sessions from one IP address, VPN or proxy use, unexpected network changes, and access from multiple devices or locations.[27][5][30]18618164disa.comtestlify.comincruiter.com
  • The cited architecture characterizes these as cheap, accurate signals that do not depend on protected-group characteristics, and recommends enabling them by default.[27]186disa.com
  • Browser-only lockdown has a hard visibility limit.our own page
  • Separate desktop apps can exclude themselves from screen capture, on-device models such as Ollama, LM Studio, and llama.cpp can run in memory without outbound network traffic, and remote-access tools can let another person drive the session at the operating-system level without touching the locked browser window.[32]198edulegit.com
  • A standard lockdown browser controls the browser tab, while the operating system can still run other applications and processes.[5]181testlify.com
  • Investigation therefore needs evidence from outside the page itself where the assessment design permits it: virtual-machine checks, detection or blocking of remote-control and screen-sharing applications such as TeamViewer and AnyDesk, overlay-application controls, IP monitoring, and behavioral typing evidence.[5]181testlify.com
  • A cited Smart Browser product claims to lock the full computer, detect virtual machines before the assessment, and block screen-sharing or screen-recording applications; those are vendor claims, not independent validation.[5]181testlify.com
  • Virtual-camera drivers can also trigger additional scrutiny because deepfake tools and artificial eye-contact tools may depend on them.[3]188aiseptor.com
  • InCruiter describes passive liveness checking with 3D depth analysis and remote photoplethysmography, intended to distinguish a live person from a photo, video loop, or deepfake overlay without requiring an explicit candidate action.[31]193aiseptor.com
  • Candidate setup can include pre-assessment image capture, camera, microphone, browser, and system-compatibility checks; continuous monitoring through images, screen, and audio samples; and a report of anomalous incidents after the assessment.[21][6]195187hackerearth.comfabrichq.ai
  • Remote-proctoring controls can produce evidence for review, including identity checks, browser restrictions, full-screen enforcement, tab and copy-paste monitoring, environment checks, dual-camera support, session recording, and question-level logs.[6]187fabrichq.ai
  • Other cited controls include secure browsers that restrict virtual-machine use and copy-paste, KYC-grade identity verification, and session monitoring that flags irregularities for human review.[24]68wearedevelopers.com

Address proxy completion, real-time coaching, and pasted answers

  • Unauthorized assistance can involve another person in the room, a remote helper communicating through earbuds or Discord, or a proxy who completes all or part of an assessment.our own page
  • The collected evidence describes proxy services offering paid “managed assessment completion,” including professional developers who specialize in clearing early coding screens.[5]181testlify.com
  • A proxy is harder to identify through in-test behavior alone because impersonation may leave no copy-paste, tab-switching, or other behavioral trace unless identity is verified throughout the session.[5]181testlify.com
  • Government-ID verification matched against a webcam capture at session start, with legal review of consent and data-handling disclosures where required, including under Illinois BIPA and in parts of the EU.[24]68wearedevelopers.com
  • Randomized webcam snapshots, with HackerEarth described as taking two snapshots per minute by default.[5]181testlify.com
  • IP-address restrictions for roles with geographic constraints.[5]181testlify.com
  • Automatic impersonation detection comparing the registered candidate with the person on camera, plus typing-pattern comparisons across sessions.[5]181testlify.com
  • Live or recorded proctoring for high-stakes stages and a short live conversation during the hiring loop.our own page
  • The evidence states that a proxy is unlikely to survive a 15-minute call with the hiring manager.[24]68wearedevelopers.com
  • For in-room help, audio monitoring can flag potential whispering, but a second person outside the camera frame remains difficult to establish conclusively without additional evidence.[5]181testlify.com
  • Threat actors may use stolen identities, deepfake interviews, voice clones, or real-time assistance to answer questions in ways that appear human.our own page
  • The collected information identifies biometric liveness detection, real-time challenge-response questions, video and audio inconsistency detection, cross-checking of background summaries against authoritative documents, linguistic analysis, and mandatory human review at decision points as layered responses.[28]116honorlock.com
  • Strategic follow-up questions can expose mismatches between an answer and the candidate’s understanding.our own page
  • Examples include asking a candidate to explain advanced terminology they used, asking about fictional libraries or frameworks, requesting spontaneous variations on a submitted solution, and requiring the candidate to defend their work in a 15-minute follow-up.[3]188aiseptor.com
  • Candidates may copy externally generated code or answers into an assessment.our own page
  • Keystroke playback can distinguish an iterative typing process from a large single insertion: a copy-paste event appears as one large insertion rather than code entered progressively.[5]181testlify.com
  • Editor playback can also reveal a solution appearing in clean blocks without the exploration, errors, debugging, or iteration normally visible in a coding process.[5]181testlify.com
  • Browser-security controls described in the collected material include blocking tab switching, external resources, and window resizing.[25]69integrityadvocate.com
  • However, restricting copy-paste can inconvenience candidates who legitimately draft in their own editor, and some senior engineers may regard the restriction as insulting.our own page
  • The proposed mitigation is to communicate the restriction in advance and reserve it for junior screens where assessment volume may justify the added friction.[24]68wearedevelopers.com
  • Copy-paste blocking can prevent candidates from moving pre-generated ChatGPT text into an answer; when pasting is allowed or tracked, the event itself can be flagged.[29]197canditech.io
  • Behavioral keystroke and mouse analysis can identify sudden shifts in typing rhythm, paste events on essay questions, and mouse movement that does not match the expected human distribution.our own page
  • In coding assessments, a paste of N tokens with no preceding typing is identified as a strong review signal.[27]186disa.com
  • Code playback can expose a process with no exploration, no errors, and no iteration, followed by complete blocks of clean code; another cited system claims to detect code written at inhuman speed or with unusually perfect structure.[5]181testlify.com
  • InCruiter states that its proctoring suite monitors clipboard activity, typing-cadence anomalies, browser extensions, and screen overlays to identify AI-tool use.[31]193aiseptor.com
  • Fabric reports analyzing more than 20 signals at once, including gaze patterns, response-timing variance, language patterns it characterizes as LLM-typical, and coherence against a candidate’s resume baseline, then producing timestamped reports for recruiter review; it claims detection in 85% of cases from its evaluations.[3]188aiseptor.com

Treat automated signals as prompts for contextual human review

  • The rationale is that AI offers instant flagging and scale, while human reviewers can interpret context and reduce false-positive harm.[6]187fabrichq.ai
  • Behavioral-pattern analysis may identify an unusual delay between a question and an unusually polished answer; code playback may reveal complete blocks of clean code appearing without exploration, errors, or iteration.[5]181testlify.com
  • Alerts alone are not proof of cheating.our own page
  • Reviewable evidence should include session recordings, snapshots, question-level activity logs, timestamps, and plain-language violation summaries so a reviewer can assess the full context before deciding.[6]187fabrichq.ai
  • AI detection in a proctoring system should surface suspicious moments for human review rather than decide misconduct on its own.our own page
  • A proposed hybrid architecture sends camera, microphone, and screen feeds to a server-side recording system, then has detectors produce timestamped events with confidence scores; a ranker selects the top suspicious moments for review.[27]186disa.com
  • Honorlock similarly describes AI alerts going to a live proctor, who reviews the situation and decides how to proceed.[29]197canditech.io
  • Reviewers should receive the surrounding 30 to 90 seconds of footage and the detector’s stated reasoning, then mark each event confirmed, dismissed, or inconclusive.our own page
  • The proposed reviewer productivity target is 60 to 90 reviewed moments per reviewer per hour.[27]186disa.com
  • Testlify’s guidance makes the same procedural point: flags alone are noise, so reviewers need recordings, snapshots, question-level logs, timestamps, and plain-language violation summaries before making a decision.[6]187fabrichq.ai
  • A defensible investigation record should log every automated flag, dismissal, and reviewer decision in a cryptographic hash chain, with the server-side recording retained as the canonical artefact.our own page
  • Browser-side recording is described as a tampering risk.[27]186disa.com
  • Head pose and gaze direction should be evaluated as changes in a candidate’s pattern, not as a verdict based on a single glance.our own page
  • One cited example is a candidate with stable gaze for 10 minutes who then looks downward for five seconds every 30 seconds.[27]186disa.com
  • Fabric likewise states that eye tracking works best as one signal among several, and distinguishes a nervous candidate looking away to think from someone repeatedly reading a hidden script through the broader behavioral pattern.[3]188aiseptor.com
  • The extract says this comparison revealed signatures of AI-assisted completion that can be flagged for investigation, but it does not specify the detection features, false-positive rate, false-negative rate, benchmark composition, AI models tested, or whether results generalize to modern multimodal models and live pre-employment assessments.[1]182assessio.com
  • The Assessio material supports using AI-completion signatures as triggers for investigation, rather than presenting a detector result as conclusive proof.our own page
  • It does not establish that those signatures are reliable enough for automatic rejection or adverse employment action.[1]182assessio.com
  • The collected material also notes that AI-writing detectors can be unreliable and cites institutional withdrawals or updates to Turnitin AI detection in 2026, a 2024 RAID benchmark, and 2026 research on false positives affecting non-native English writers. This evidence is about academic writing detection, not pre-employment skills tests, but it raises a directly relevant caution against treating automated AI-use flags as dispositive without review and corroboration.[9]191meazurelearning.com
  • Human involvement may improve context-sensitive handling of incidental issues, such as a forgotten phone, connected second monitor, or open browser tab, because trained reviewers can address problems before an exam or interpret them with nuance afterward.[15]150pin.com
  • The collected information does not quantify how often these events are innocent, how often they lead to false accusations, or how candidate experience differs between live, recorded, automated, and no-proctoring approaches.our own page
  • The material advises evaluating reasonable accommodations, transparent candidate-facing interfaces, hardware burden, and technical friction because invasive proctoring and excessive false positives can damage employer brand.our own page
  • It does not provide completion-rate, abandonment-rate, disability-access, demographic-disparity, or candidate-satisfaction data for competing assessment-integrity designs.[31]193aiseptor.com
  • Yet automated flags are not equivalent to proof of misconduct.our own page
  • In AI-only and “pop-in” proctoring models, the collected material reports that up to 30% of flags are false positives, including flags caused by routine background noise or poor lighting, and that only about 10% of flags are reviewed by a human.[15]150pin.com
  • A human-involved model is described as reviewing every session in real time or shortly afterward, which can both identify genuine violations and dismiss false alarms.[15]150pin.com
  • In one client example, student satisfaction rose from 62% to 94% within a year of moving from an automated model to a human-involved proctoring solution, though this evidence comes from an education setting rather than pre-employment testing.[15]150pin.com
  • Because flags can be mistaken, suspected AI use should trigger verification rather than automatic rejection.our own page
  • The collected material’s fairness protocol for AI-detector flags recommends treating a score as a prompt rather than a verdict; comparing the output with known prior work, outlines, version history, and revision patterns; asking process questions; recording the reasoning; and stating the AI-use policy in advance.[9]191meazurelearning.com

Weigh proctoring's deterrence evidence and remaining gaps

  • One cited study found dishonest behavior in 70% of unproctored student exams versus 15% where proctoring was in place.[15]150pin.com
  • Across three human-led proctoring service lines, 7 in 10 unpermitted resources were reportedly identified and addressed before the exam began, which the source links to fewer interruptions, pauses, restarts, and follow-up investigations.[15]150pin.com
  • One cited study found dishonest behavior in 70% of unproctored exams, compared with 15% when proctoring was present.our own page
  • This is evidence that observed misconduct rates can vary sharply with the assessment’s supervision model, though the excerpt concerns exams generally and does not establish that all dishonest behavior was AI-assisted or occurred in employment testing.[15]150pin.com
  • Across three human-led proctoring service lines, a proctoring provider reports that 7 in 10 unpermitted resources are identified and addressed before the exam begins.our own page
  • The reported mechanism is both deterrence and earlier human interpretation of issues such as a phone left on a desk, a plugged-in second monitor, or an open browser tab.[15]150pin.com
  • A human-proctoring source cites a study in which 70% of students engaged in dishonest behavior in unproctored exams, compared with 15% when proctoring was present.our own page
  • This is strong comparative evidence that proctoring can deter misconduct, but it concerns students rather than job candidates and does not isolate generative-AI use from other forms of dishonesty.[15]150pin.com
  • The same source reports that, across three human-led proctoring service lines, 7 in 10 unpermitted resources were identified and addressed before the exam began.our own page
  • The stated practical effects were fewer interruptions, pauses or restarts, follow-up issues, and formal investigations.our own page
  • The collected information repeatedly argues for layered controls, including proctoring, identity verification, liveness verification, deepfake detection, behavioral analysis, and human review.our own page
  • Yet it provides no independently validated comparison of these controls’ sensitivity, specificity, false-positive rate, false-negative rate, cost, accessibility effects, or performance against particular AI-enabled fraud methods.[2]184linkedin.com
  • One procurement framework advises organizations to pilot known fraud scenarios and request false-positive and false-negative rates, emphasizing that a tool that incorrectly flags honest candidates can be as costly as one that misses fraud.our own page
  • This is a useful evaluation standard, but the extract does not provide published rates for any vendor or modality.[31]193aiseptor.com

How does AI perform against human candidates in Assessio’s benchmark?no keyword

  • Assessio also benchmarked AI against more than 10,000 human candidates and reports that AI achieved 44% accuracy on figural questions, while performing better on verbal and numerical items.our own page
